## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: Solid Mechanics and Thermomechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the constitutive relationship between stress, strain, and temperature, which is central to materials science and solid mechanics for describing thermomechanical material behavior, phase transformations, and temperature-dependent plasticity or elasticity.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Thermoelastic Hooke's law: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with temperature-dependent modulus)
- Thermal strain offset model: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * T)**c2 (stress response shifted by thermal expansion)
- Ludwik-Hollomon hardening with thermal softening: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 * exp(c3 * T) (plastic flow stress decreasing with temperature)
- Polynomial strain hardening with linear thermal coupling: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * T * epsilon (geometric nonlinearity under thermal load)
- Power-law creep approximation: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (diffusion-controlled steady-state deformation)
- Hyperelastic neo-Hookean type: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (epsilon - epsilon**(-2)) (large deformation rubber-like response)
- Johnson-Cook simplified plasticity: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T) (empirical metal plasticity without strain rate)
- Thermally activated dislocation motion: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * T * sinh(c2 * epsilon) (Eyring-type rate-independent flow stress)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus → Linear/affine scaling of strain term by T: (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon
- Thermal strain offset (zero-stress shift) → Horizontal translation of strain axis proportional to temperature: f(epsilon - c * T)
- Thermally activated dislocation motion → Stress proportional to temperature times hyperbolic sine or logarithm of strain: c * T * sinh(c * epsilon)
- Progressive plastic hardening with thermal softening → Power-law or exponential strain hardening multiplied by decaying thermal factor: (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(-c3 * T)
- Large-deformation geometric nonlinearity → Difference of positive and inverse powers of strain: epsilon - epsilon**(-2)
- Damage accumulation and strength degradation → Multiplicative decay of stress capacity with both strain and temperature: c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(-c2 * T)
- Phase-transformation volume change coupling → Cross-product or rational interaction between strain and temperature: c * epsilon * T / (1 + c * epsilon)
- Low-strain logarithmic response (dislocation pinning) → Logarithmic dependence on strain scaled by thermal factor: c * log(1 + c * epsilon) * (1 + c * T)

Let $E = \epsilon$, $T = T$.
GT = $A E^2 + A E (-B (T - C) + 1) + D (T - C) \log(E + 1)$
where:
$A = 11.11905375829476$
$B = 0.09195630170381391$
$C = 352.0084637124087$
$D = 4.3699183274837985$

Expand GT:
$= A E^2 - A B E (T - C) + A E + D (T - C) \log(E + 1)$
$= A E^2 + A E - A B E T + A B E C + D T \log(E + 1) - D C \log(E + 1)$
Group by terms involving $T$ and terms independent of $T$:
$= T [ -A B E + D \log(E + 1) ] + [ A E^2 + A E + A B C E - D C \log(E + 1) ]$
$= T [ D \log(E + 1) - A B E ] + [ A E^2 + (A + A B C) E - D C \log(E + 1) ]$

So the GT is a linear function of $T$:
$GT = T \cdot f(E) + g(E)$

$f(E) = D \log(E + 1) - A B E$
$g(E) = A E^2 + (A + A B C) E - D C \log(E + 1)$

### Ground Truth Analysis
The Ground Truth (GT) expression is:
`c0*epsilon**c1 + c2*epsilon*(-c3*(T - c4) + c5) + c6*(T - c7)*log(epsilon + c8)`
Substituting the given numerical constants ($c_1=2, c_8=1$) and expanding algebraically:
`GT = A*epsilon**2 + A*epsilon*(-B*(T - C) + 1) + D*(T - C)*log(epsilon + 1)`
where $A, B, C, D$ are fixed positive constants.
Expanding and grouping by powers of $T$:
`GT = T * [ D*log(epsilon + 1) - A*B*epsilon ] + [ A*epsilon**2 + (A + A*B*C)*epsilon - D*C*log(epsilon + 1) ]`
**Key Structural Features of GT:**
1. Strictly **linear in T** (no $\sqrt{T}$, $T^2$, $T^{1/3}$, $\log(T)$, $\exp(T)$, etc.).
2. Contains exactly these basis functions multiplied by $T$ or constants: `T*log(epsilon+1)`, `T*epsilon`, `epsilon**2`, `epsilon`, `log(epsilon+1)`.
3. No trigonometric (`sin`, `cos`), exponential (`exp`), or fractional power terms.

### Candidate Verification
We evaluate each candidate against these strict structural requirements. Candidates containing `exp`, `sin`, `cos`, `sqrt(T)`, `log(T)`, `T**(1/3)`, or missing required basis terms (`T*log(epsilon+1)` or `T*epsilon`) are immediately rejected due to linear independence of basis functions.
